=> [{:title=>"RMS Objects To Support For LLVM's Debugger In GNU Emacs's Gud.el", :link=>"http://rss.slashdot.org/~r/Slashdot/slashdot/~3/q4E0Ummr__A/story01.htm", :summary=>"An anonymous reader writes with the news that Richard Stallman is upset over the prospect of GNU Emacs's Grand Unified Debugger (Gud.el) supporting LLVM's LLDB debugger. Stallman says it looks like there is a systematic effort to attack GNU packages and calls for the GNU to respond strategically. He wrote his concerns to the mailing list after a patch emerged that would optionally support LLDB alongside GDB as an alternative debugger for Emacs. Other Emacs developers discounted RMS' claims by saying Emacs supports Windows and OS X, so why not support a BSD-licensed compiler/debugger? The Emacs maintainer has called the statements irrelevant and won't affect their decision to merge the LLDB support.<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a src=\"//feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Slashdot/slashdot/~4/q4E0Ummr__A\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>"}, {:title=>"AP Test's Recursion Examples: An Exercise In Awkardness", :link=>"http://rss.slashdot.org/~r/Slashdot/slashdot/~3/8LhJzR3Wz5U/story01.htm", :summary=>"theodp writes Yet another example of how AP exams are loaded with poor coding practices,\" quipped Alfred Thompson, referring to a recursive code example that prints the numbers 0 to 6, which was posted to the (closed) AP Computer Science Facebook group. \"We are often forced to use code examples that are not ideal coding practice,\" Thompson notes. \"We do that to make things clear and to demonstrate specific concepts in a sort of isolation that we might not normally use. We seem to do that a lot with recursion because the examples that require recursion tend to be fairly complex.\" So, while asking students to use recursion instead of a loop to print '0123456' serves the purpose of teaching recursion, Thompson opines that it's also a poor example of code practice. \"Someone raised on functional programming where recursion is a pretty standard way of doing looping might disagree of course,\" he adds. \"There is a saying that when all you have is a hammer all your problems look like nails. This seems, in a way, to be the case with recursion and loops. If your first tool of choice (or what you have learned first) for iteration is loops you tend not to think of recursion as a solution. Similarly if you start with recursion (as is common with functional programming) you are a lot more likely to look at recursion as a tool for iteration.\" So, do you tend to embrace or eschew recursion in your programming?<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=AP+Test's+Recursion+Examples%3A+An+Exercise+In+Awkardness%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1DThznr\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fdevelopers.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F08%2F1935257%2Fap-tests-recursion-examples-an-exercise-in-awkardness%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://developers.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/1935257/ap-tests-recursion-examples-an-exercise-in-awkardness?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://developers.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/1935257/ap-tests-recursion-examples-an-exercise-in-awkardness?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6934629&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; Now Rick Broida reports at Cnet that you can get Google Earth Pro absolutely free. All you have to do is download the installer, run it, then sign in using your e-mail address (as your username) and license code GEPFREE. Features include: Advanced measurements: Measure parking lots and land developments with polygon area measure, or determine affected radius with circle measure; High-resolution printing: Print images up to 4,800 x 3,200 pixel resolution; Exclusive pro data layers with Demographics and traffic count; Spreadsheet import: Ingest up to 2,500 addresses at a time, assigning place marks and style templates in bulk; and Movie-Maker: Export Windows Media and QuickTime HD movies, up to 1,920x1,080-pixel resolution. If you've ever been involved in a property dispute, you'll know how acrimonious they can get. Google Earth Pro includes parcel data that definitively defines property boundaries. \"Do you really need this? Probably not, as Pro was created with business/enterprise users in mind,\" writes Broida. \"Let's be honest, [Google Earth Pro has] entertainment value that's virtually impossible to measure.\"<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=Google+Earth+Pro+Now+Available+Free%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1DablkN\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fsearch.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F08%2F1854255%2Fgoogle-earth-pro-now-available-free%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://search.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/1854255/google-earth-pro-now-available-free?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://search.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/1854255/google-earth-pro-now-available-free?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6934523&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; The idea is for an annual or bi-annual Turing Championship consisting of three to five different challenging tasks. A recent workshop at the 2015 AAAI Conference of Artificial Intelligence was chaired by Gary Marcus, a professor of psychology at New York University. His opinion is that the Turing Test had reached its expiry date and has become \"an exercise in deception and evasion.\" Marcus points out: the real value of the Turing Test comes from the sense of competition it sparks amongst programmers and engineers which has motivated the new initiative for a multi-task competition. The one of the tasks is based on Winograd Schemas. This requires participants to grasp the meaning of sentences that are easy for humans to understand through their knowledge of the world. One simple example is: \"The trophy would not fit in the brown suitcase because it was too big. What was too big?\" Another suggestion is for the program to answer questions about a TV program: No existing program &mdash; not Watson, not Goostman, not Siri &mdash; can currently come close to doing what any bright, real teenager can do: watch an episode of \"The Simpsons,\" and tell us when to laugh. Another is called the \"Ikea\" challenge and asks for robots to co-operate with humans to build flat-pack furniture. This involves interpreting written instructions, choosing the right piece, and holding it in just the right position for a human teammate. This at least is a useful skill that might encourage us to welcome machines into our homes.<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=Replacing+the+Turing+Test%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1DtEvvO\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fhardware.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F08%2F1751201%2Freplacing-the-turing-test%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://hardware.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/1751201/replacing-the-turing-test?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://hardware.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/1751201/replacing-the-turing-test?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6934345&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; SuSE in the early days, after that either Debian or, more recently, Ubuntu, if I want something to click on. What really bugs me is, that every time I make a new setup, either as a virtual machine, on concrete hardware or a remote host, I go through 1-2 hours of getting the basics of a web-centric system up and running. That includes setting PHP config options to usable things, setting up vhosts on Apache (always an adventure), configging mod_rewrite, installing extra CLI stuff like Emacs (yeah, I'm from that camp) walking through the basic 10-15 steps of setting up MySQL or some other DB, etc. ... You get the picture. What has me wondering is this: Since Linux is deeply entrenched in the field of server-side web, with LAMP being it's powerhouse, I was wondering if there aren't any distros that cover exactly this sort of thing. You know, automatic allocation of memory in the runtime settings, ready-made Apache http/https/sftp/ftp setup, PHP all ready to go, etc. What are your experiences and is there something that covers this? Would you think there's a need for this sort of thing and would you base it of Debian or something else? If you do web-dev, how do you do it? Prepareted scripts for setup? Anything else? ... Ideas, unkown LAMP distros and opinions please.\"<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=Ask+Slashdot%3A+Is+There+a+Web+Development+Linux+Distro%3F%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1yX3iTE\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fask.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F08%2F0650246%2Fask-slashdot-is-there-a-web-development-linux-distro%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://ask.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/0650246/ask-slashdot-is-there-a-web-development-linux-distro?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://ask.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/0650246/ask-slashdot-is-there-a-web-development-linux-distro?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6931947&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; It does not limit physician-assisted death to those suffering a terminal illness. The court agreed with the trial judge \"that a permissive regime with properly designed and administered safeguards was capable of protecting vulnerable people from abuse and error. :link=>"http://rss.slashdot.org/~r/Slashdot/slashdot/~3/AkR-Go-hb80/story01.htm", :summary=>"Inland parts of Oregon and Washington, as well as Idaho, have experienced a strange, murky rain today that contains what seems to be volcanic ash, though ash from which volcano isn't completely clear. Experts said they are checking out several possible explanations including a recent volcanic eruption in Mexico and one in Russia. The weather service said the rainstorm may have passed through some dust or volcanic ash as it moved west. Walla Walla County's emergency management staff posted a statement on its Facebook page that the ash is likely from Volcano Shiveluch in Kamchatka Krai, Russia, some 3,000 miles away. Volcano Shiveluch spewed an ash plume about 22,000 feet high in late January, the statement said.... CNN meteorologist Derek Van Dam, meanwhile, pointed to an eruption Wednesday of a volcano in southwestern Colima, Mexico, as another potential source of the dirty rain. That volcano is more than 2,000 miles away from the region. Time points out that other theories include leftover ash from last year&rsquo;s wildfires in Oregon in Idaho.<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=Mystery+Ash+Clouds+Rain+In+Parts+of+Washington%2C+Oregon%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1CGxecR\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fscience.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F08%2F0042241%2Fmystery-ash-clouds-rain-in-parts-of-washington-oregon%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://science.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/0042241/mystery-ash-clouds-rain-in-parts-of-washington-oregon?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://science.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/0042241/mystery-ash-clouds-rain-in-parts-of-washington-oregon?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6929363&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; Over time, the fact that the Moon's orbit is elliptical, and that it moves faster at perigee and slower at apogee means that up to another 9% is visible over the course of many years. The observed \"rocking\" and growing/shrinking of the Moon over time is known as lunar libration, an incredibly interesting phenomenon. But now, for the first time, we've been able to visualize how the Earth appears to move as seen from above the far side of the Moon.<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=Earth's+Libration+Visualized+For+the+First+Time+Above+the+Moon's+Far+Side%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1zjrgHD\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fscience.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F07%2F2337213%2Fearths-libration-visualized-for-the-first-time-above-the-moons-far-side%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://science.slashdot.org/story/15/02/07/2337213/earths-libration-visualized-for-the-first-time-above-the-moons-far-side?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://science.slashdot.org/story/15/02/07/2337213/earths-libration-visualized-for-the-first-time-above-the-moons-far-side?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6928943&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; ISPs then have to comply with the request within 24 hours. ISPs will be able to request compensation from the French government for any extra costs incurred in blocking the sites. Users who navigate to a site 'to which access is prohibited will be led to an informational page from the Ministry of the Interior,' the text of the decree said. The informational page will list the grounds for the blocking as well as any possibly remedies. Every quarter, French authorities will check whether the blocked pages still contain the offending material. If not, then the authorities will contact ISPs, which will have to unblock the sites, again within 24 hours.<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=Sites+Featuring+%22Terrorism%22+Or+%22Child+Pornography%22+To+Be+Blocked+In+France%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1A0e6X4\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fyro.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F07%2F2244243%2Fsites-featuring-terrorism-or-child-pornography-to-be-blocked-in-france%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://yro.slashdot.org/story/15/02/07/2244243/sites-featuring-terrorism-or-child-pornography-to-be-blocked-in-france?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://yro.slashdot.org/story/15/02/07/2244243/sites-featuring-terrorism-or-child-pornography-to-be-blocked-in-france?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6928647&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; It measures a mere 6 millimeters thick, or 0.24 inches and change. That's 0.1mm slimmer than Apple's iPad Air 2 and 1.5mm flatter than the iPad mini 3, giving Dell full bragging rights, even if by a hair. Dell also opted for an Intel Atom Z3580 processor under the hood, clocked at up to 2.3GHz. This quad-core part is built on Intel's 22nm Moorefield microarchitecture. Compared to its Bay Trail predecessor, Moorefield comes in a smaller package with superior thermal attributes, as well as better graphics performance, courtesy of its PowerVR G6430 graphics core. The Venue 8 7000 also features one of the best 8-inch OLED displays on the market, with edge-to-edge glass and a 2560x1600 resolution. Finally, the Venue 8 7000 is also the first to integrate Intel's RealSense Snapshot Depth Camera, which offers interesting re-focusing and stereoscopic effects, with potentially other, more interesting use cases down the road. Performance-wise, the Venue 8 7000 is solid enough though not a speedster, putting out metrics in the benchmarks that place it in the middle of the pack of premium tablets on the market currently.\"<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=Dell+Venue+8+7000%2C+%22World's+Thinnest+Tablet%22+With+Intel+Moorefield+Atom+Reviewed%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1IptnV9\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fhardware.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F07%2F1622212%2Fdell-venue-8-7000-worlds-thinnest-tablet-with-intel-moorefield-atom-reviewed%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://hardware.slashdot.org/story/15/02/07/1622212/dell-venue-8-7000-worlds-thinnest-tablet-with-intel-moorefield-atom-reviewed?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://hardware.slashdot.org/story/15/02/07/1622212/dell-venue-8-7000-worlds-thinnest-tablet-with-intel-moorefield-atom-reviewed?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6926119&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; We seem to do that a lot with recursion because the examples that require recursion tend to be fairly complex.\" So, while asking students to use recursion instead of a loop to print '0123456' serves the purpose of teaching recursion, Thompson opines that it's also a poor example of code practice. \"Someone raised on functional programming where recursion is a pretty standard way of doing looping might disagree of course,\" he adds. \"There is a saying that when all you have is a hammer all your problems look like nails. This seems, in a way, to be the case with recursion and loops. If your first tool of choice (or what you have learned first) for iteration is loops you tend not to think of recursion as a solution. Similarly if you start with recursion (as is common with functional programming) you are a lot more likely to look at recursion as a tool for iteration.\" So, do you tend to embrace or eschew :link=>"http://rss.slashdot.org/~r/Slashdot/slashdot/~3/waQrMrBHDpE/story01.htm", :summary=>"MojoKid (1002251) writes \"Dell recently launched their Android-based Venue 8 7000 slate, claiming it's the \"world's thinnest\" tablet. It measures a mere 6 millimeters thick, or 0.24 inches and change. That's 0.1mm slimmer than Apple's iPad Air 2 and 1.5mm flatter than the iPad mini 3, giving Dell full bragging rights, even if by a hair. Dell also opted for an Intel Atom Z3580 processor under the hood, clocked at up to 2.3GHz. This quad-core part is built on Intel's 22nm Moorefield microarchitecture. Compared to its Bay Trail predecessor, Moorefield comes in a smaller package with superior thermal attributes, as well as better graphics performance, courtesy of its PowerVR G6430 graphics core. The Venue 8 7000 also features one of the best 8-inch OLED displays on the market, with edge-to-edge glass and a 2560x1600 resolution. Finally, the Venue 8 7000 is also the first to integrate Intel's RealSense Snapshot Depth Camera, which offers interesting re-focusing and stereoscopic effects, with potentially other, more interesting use cases down the road. Performance-wise, the Venue 8 7000 is solid enough though not a speedster, putting out metrics in the benchmarks that place it in the middle of the pack of premium tablets on the market currently.\"<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=Dell+Venue+8+7000%2C+%22Word's+Thinnest+Tablet%22+With+Intel+Moorefield+Atom%2C+Reviewed%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1IptnV9\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fhardware.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F07%2F1622212%2Fdell-venue-8-7000-words-thinnest-tablet-with-intel-moorefield-atom-reviewed%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://hardware.slashdot.org/story/15/02/07/1622212/dell-venue-8-7000-words-thinnest-tablet-with-intel-moorefield-atom-reviewed?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://hardware.slashdot.org/story/15/02/07/1622212/dell-venue-8-7000-words-thinnest-tablet-with-intel-moorefield-atom-reviewed?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6926119&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; The observed \"rocking\" and growing/shrinking of the Moon over time is known as lunar libration, an incredibly interesting phenomenon. Volcano Shiveluch spewed an ash plume about 22,000 feet high in late January, the statement said.... CNN meteorologist Derek Van Dam, meanwhile, pointed to an eruption Wednesday of a volcano in southwestern Colima, Mexico, as another potential source of the dirty rain. Think about it: Dozens of people\nsweating in close proximity, running on conveyor belts going nowhere, lifting\nand dropping heavy objects for no reason.\n\n\n-- Read more on ScientificAmerican.com\n\n"}, {:title=>"Replacing the Turing Test", :link=>"http://rss.slashdot.org/~r/Slashdot/slashdot/~3/j2aAUur8xpY/story01.htm", :summary=>"mikejuk writes A plan is afoot to replace the Turing test as a measure of a computer's ability to think. The idea is for an annual or bi-annual Turing Championship consisting of three to five different challenging tasks. A recent workshop at the 2015 AAAI Conference of Artificial Intelligence was chaired by Gary Marcus, a professor of psychology at New York University. His opinion is that the Turing Test had reached its expiry date and has become \"an exercise in deception and evasion.\" Marcus points out: the real value of the Turing Test comes from the sense of competition it sparks amongst programmers and engineers which has motivated the new initiative for a multi-task competition. The one of the tasks is based on Winograd Schemas. This requires participants to grasp the meaning of sentences that are easy for humans to understand through their knowledge of the world. One simple example is: \"The trophy would not fit in the brown suitcase because it was too big. What was too big?\" Another suggestion is for the program to answer questions about a TV program: No existing program &mdash; not Watson, not Goostman, not Siri &mdash; can currently come close to doing what any bright, real teenager can do: watch an episode of \"The Simpsons,\" and tell us when to laugh. Another is called the \"Ikea\" challenge and asks for robots to co-operate with humans to build flat-pack furniture. This involves interpreting written instructions, choosing the right piece, and holding it in just the right position for a human teammate. This at least is a useful skill that might encourage us to welcome machines into our homes.<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=Replacing+the+Turing+Test%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1DtEvvO\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fhardware.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F08%2F1751201%2Freplacing-the-turing-test%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://hardware.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/1751201/replacing-the-turing-test?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://hardware.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/1751201/replacing-the-turing-test?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6934345&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; ISPs then have to comply with the request within 24 hours. ISPs will be able to request compensation from the French government for any extra costs incurred in blocking the sites. Users who navigate to a site 'to which access is prohibited will be led to an informational page from the Ministry of the Interior,' the text of the decree said. The informational page will list the grounds for the blocking as well as any possibly remedies. Every quarter, French authorities will check whether the blocked pages still contain the offending material. If not, then the authorities will contact ISPs, which will have to unblock the sites, again within 24 hours.<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=Sites+Featuring+%22Terrorism%22+Or+%22Child+Pornography%22+To+Be+Blocked+In+France%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1A0e6X4\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fyro.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F07%2F2244243%2Fsites-featuring-terrorism-or-child-pornography-to-be-blocked-in-france%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://yro.slashdot.org/story/15/02/07/2244243/sites-featuring-terrorism-or-child-pornography-to-be-blocked-in-france?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://yro.slashdot.org/story/15/02/07/2244243/sites-featuring-terrorism-or-child-pornography-to-be-blocked-in-france?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6928647&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; We seem to do that a lot with recursion because the examples that require recursion tend to be fairly complex.\" So, while asking students to use recursion instead of a loop to print '0123456' serves the purpose of teaching recursion, Thompson opines that it's also a poor example of code practice. \"Someone raised on functional programming where recursion is a pretty standard way of doing looping might disagree of course,\" he adds. \"There is a saying that when all you have is a hammer all your problems look like nails. This seems, in a way, to be the case with recursion and loops. If your first tool of choice (or what you have learned first) for iteration is loops you tend not to think of recursion as a solution. Similarly if you start with recursion (as is common with functional programming) you are a lot more likely to look at recursion as a tool for iteration.\" So, do you tend to embrace or eschew What really bugs me is, that every time I make a new setup, either as a virtual machine, on concrete hardware or a remote host, I go through 1-2 hours of getting the basics of a web-centric system up and running. That includes setting PHP config options to usable things, setting up vhosts on Apache (always an adventure), configging mod_rewrite, installing extra CLI stuff like Emacs (yeah, I'm from that camp) walking through the basic 10-15 steps of setting up MySQL or some other DB, etc. ... You get the picture. What has me wondering is this: Since Linux is deeply entrenched in the field of server-side web, with LAMP being it's powerhouse, I was wondering if there aren't any distros that cover exactly this sort of thing. You know, automatic allocation of memory in the runtime settings, ready-made Apache http/https/sftp/ftp setup, PHP all ready to go, etc. What are your experiences and is there something that covers this? Would you think there's a need for this sort of thing and would you base it of Debian or something else? If you do web-dev, how do you do it? Prepareted scripts for setup? Anything else? ... Ideas, unkown LAMP distros and opinions please.\"<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" :link=>"http://rss.slashdot.org/~r/Slashdot/slashdot/~3/waQrMrBHDpE/story01.htm", :summary=>"MojoKid (1002251) writes \"Dell recently launched their Android-based Venue 8 7000 slate, claiming it's the \"world's thinnest\" tablet. It measures a mere 6 millimeters thick, or 0.24 inches and change. That's 0.1mm slimmer than Apple's iPad Air 2 and 1.5mm flatter than the iPad mini 3, giving Dell full bragging rights, even if by a hair. Dell also opted for an Intel Atom Z3580 processor under the hood, clocked at up to 2.3GHz. This quad-core part is built on Intel's 22nm Moorefield microarchitecture. Compared to its Bay Trail predecessor, Moorefield comes in a smaller package with superior thermal attributes, as well as better graphics performance, courtesy of its PowerVR G6430 graphics core. The Venue 8 7000 also features one of the best 8-inch OLED displays on the market, with edge-to-edge glass and a 2560x1600 resolution. Finally, the Venue 8 7000 is also the first to integrate Intel's RealSense Snapshot Depth Camera, which offers interesting re-focusing and stereoscopic effects, with potentially other, more interesting use cases down the road. Performance-wise, the Venue 8 7000 is solid enough though not a speedster, putting out metrics in the benchmarks that place it in the middle of the pack of premium tablets on the market currently.\"<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=Dell+Venue+8+7000%2C+%22Word's+Thinnest+Tablet%22+With+Intel+Moorefield+Atom%2C+Reviewed%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1IptnV9\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fhardware.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F07%2F1622212%2Fdell-venue-8-7000-words-thinnest-tablet-with-intel-moorefield-atom-reviewed%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://hardware.slashdot.org/story/15/02/07/1622212/dell-venue-8-7000-words-thinnest-tablet-with-intel-moorefield-atom-reviewed?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://hardware.slashdot.org/story/15/02/07/1622212/dell-venue-8-7000-words-thinnest-tablet-with-intel-moorefield-atom-reviewed?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6926119&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; Over time, the fact that the Moon's orbit is elliptical, and that it moves faster at perigee and slower at apogee means that up to another 9% is visible over the course of many years. Stallman says it looks like there is a systematic effort to attack GNU packages and calls for the GNU to respond strategically. He wrote his concerns to the mailing list after a patch emerged that would optionally support LLDB alongside GDB as an alternative debugger for Emacs. Other Emacs developers discounted RMS' claims by saying Emacs supports Windows and OS X, so why not support a BSD-licensed compiler/debugger? The Emacs maintainer has called the statements irrelevant and won't affect their decision to merge the LLDB support.<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=RMS+Objects+To+Support+For+LLVM's+Debugger+In+GNU+Emacs's+Gud.el%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1KxwGqU\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fdevelopers.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F08%2F210241%2Frms-objects-to-support-for-llvms-debugger-in-gnu-emacss-gudel%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://developers.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/210241/rms-objects-to-support-for-llvms-debugger-in-gnu-emacss-gudel?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://developers.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/210241/rms-objects-to-support-for-llvms-debugger-in-gnu-emacss-gudel?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6934855&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; The idea is for an annual or bi-annual Turing Championship consisting of three to five different challenging tasks. A recent workshop at the 2015 AAAI Conference of Artificial Intelligence was chaired by Gary Marcus, a professor of psychology at New York University. His opinion is that the Turing Test had reached its expiry date and has become \"an exercise in deception and evasion.\" Marcus points out: the real value of the Turing Test comes from the sense of competition it sparks amongst programmers and engineers which has motivated the new initiative for a multi-task competition. The one of the tasks is based on Winograd Schemas. This requires participants to grasp the meaning of sentences that are easy for humans to understand through their knowledge of the world. One simple example is: \"The trophy would not fit in the brown suitcase because it was too big. What was too big?\" Another suggestion is for the program to answer questions about a TV program: No existing program &mdash; not Watson, not Goostman, not Siri &mdash; can currently come close to doing what any bright, real teenager can do: watch an episode of \"The Simpsons,\" and tell us when to laugh. Another is called the \"Ikea\" challenge and asks for robots to co-operate with humans to build flat-pack furniture. This involves interpreting written instructions, choosing the right piece, and holding it in just the right position for a human teammate. This at least is a useful skill that might encourage us to welcome machines into our homes.<p><div class=\"share_submission\" style=\"position:relative;\"> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://twitter.com/home?status=Replacing+the+Turing+Test%3A+http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F1DtEvvO\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/twitter_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"slashpop\" href=\"http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fhardware.slashdot.org%2Fstory%2F15%2F02%2F08%2F1751201%2Freplacing-the-turing-test%3Futm_source%3Dslashdot%26utm_medium%3Dfacebook\"><img src=\"http://a.fsdn.com/sd/facebook_icon_large.png\"></a> <a class=\"nobg\" href=\"http://plus.google.com/share?url=http://hardware.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/1751201/replacing-the-turing-test?utm_source=slashdot&amp;utm_medium=googleplus\" onclick=\"javascript:window.open(this.href,'', 'menubar=no,toolbar=no,resizable=yes,scrollbars=yes,height=600,width=600');return false;\"><img src=\"http://www.gstatic.com/images/icons/gplus-16.png\" alt=\"Share on Google+\"/></a> </div></p><p><a href=\"http://hardware.slashdot.org/story/15/02/08/1751201/replacing-the-turing-test?utm_source=rss1.0moreanon&amp;utm_medium=feed\">Read more of this story</a> at Slashdot.</p><iframe src=\"http://slashdot.org/slashdot-it.pl?op=discuss&amp;id=6934345&amp;smallembed=1\" style=\"height: 300px; ISPs then have to comply with the request within 24 hours. ISPs will be able to request compensation from the French government for any extra costs incurred in blocking the sites. Users who navigate to a site 'to which access is prohibited will be led to an informational page from the Ministry of the Interior,' the text of the decree said. The informational page will list the grounds for the blocking as well as any possibly remedies. Every quarter, French authorities will check whether the blocked pages still contain the offending material. #<Axlsx::Cell:0x007fc1e8a00878 @row=#<Axlsx::Row:0x007fc1e8a01200 ...>, @value="theodp writes Yet another example of how AP exams are loaded with poor coding practices,&quot; quipped Alfred Thompson, referring to a recursive code example that prints the numbers 0 to 6, which was posted to the (closed) AP Computer Science Facebook group. &quot;We are often forced to use code examples that are not ideal coding practice,&quot; Thompson notes. &quot;We do that to make things clear and to demonstrate specific concepts in a sort of isolation that we might not normally use. We seem to do that a lot with recursion because the examples that require recursion tend to be fairly complex.&quot; So, while asking students to use recursion instead of a loop to print &#39;0123456&#39; serves the purpose of teaching recursion, Thompson opines that it&#39;s also a poor example of code practice. &quot;Someone raised on functional programming where recursion is a pretty standard way of doing looping might disagree of course,&quot; he adds. &quot;There is a saying that when all you have is a hammer all your problems look like nails. This seems, in a way, to be the case with recursion and loops. If your first tool of choice (or what you have learned first) for iteration is loops you tend not to think of recursion as a solution. Similarly if you start with recursion (as is common with functional programming) you are a lot more likely to look at recursion as a tool for iteration.&quot; So, do you tend to embrace or eschew #<Axlsx::Cell:0x007fc1e89e9178 @row=#<Axlsx::Row:0x007fc1e89e9b78 ...>, @value="Qbertino writes I&#39;ve been a linux user for more than 15 years now and in the last ten I&#39;ve done basically all my non-trivial web development on Linux. SuSE in the early days, after that either Debian or, more recently, Ubuntu, if I want something to click on. What really bugs me is, that every time I make a new setup, either as a virtual machine, on concrete hardware or a remote host, I go through 1-2 hours of getting the basics of a web-centric system up and running. That includes setting PHP config options to usable things, setting up vhosts on Apache (always an adventure), configging mod_rewrite, installing extra CLI stuff like Emacs (yeah, I&#39;m from that camp) walking through the basic 10-15 steps of setting up MySQL or some other DB, etc. ... You get the picture. What has me wondering is this: Since Linux is deeply entrenched in the field of server-side web, with LAMP being it&#39;s powerhouse, I was wondering if there aren&#39;t any distros that cover exactly this sort of thing. You know, automatic allocation of memory in the runtime settings, ready-made Apache http/https/sftp/ftp setup, PHP all ready to go, etc. What are your experiences and is there something that covers this? Would you think there&#39;s a need for this sort of thing and would you base it of Debian or something else? If you do web-dev, how do you do it? Prepareted scripts for setup? Anything else? ... Ideas, unkown LAMP distros and opinions please.&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;share_submission&quot; style=&quot;position:relative;&quot;&gt; &lt;a class=&quot;slashpop&quot; &quot;world&#39;s thinnest&quot; tablet. It measures a mere 6 millimeters thick, or 0.24 inches and change. That&#39;s 0.1mm slimmer than Apple&#39;s iPad Air 2 and 1.5mm flatter than the iPad mini 3, giving Dell full bragging rights, even if by a hair. Dell also opted for an Intel Atom Z3580 processor under the hood, clocked at up to 2.3GHz. This quad-core part is built on Intel&#39;s 22nm Moorefield microarchitecture. Compared to its Bay Trail predecessor, Moorefield comes in a smaller package with superior thermal attributes, as well as better graphics performance, courtesy of its PowerVR G6430 graphics core. The Venue 8 7000 also features one of the best 8-inch OLED displays on the market, with edge-to-edge glass and a 2560x1600 resolution. Finally, the Venue 8 7000 is also the first to integrate Intel&#39;s RealSense Snapshot Depth Camera, which offers interesting re-focusing and stereoscopic effects, with potentially other, more interesting use cases down the road. Performance-wise, the Venue 8 7000 is solid enough though not a speedster, putting out metrics in the benchmarks that place it in the middle of the pack of premium tablets on the market Finally, the Venue 8 7000 is also the first to integrate Intel&#39;s RealSense Snapshot Depth Camera, which offers interesting re-focusing and stereoscopic effects, with potentially other, more interesting use cases down the road. Performance-wise, the Venue 8 7000 is solid enough though not a speedster, putting out metrics in the benchmarks that place it in the middle of the pack of premium tablets on the market #<Axlsx::Cell:0x007fc1e89bb7f0 @row=#<Axlsx::Row:0x007fc1e89c01d8 ...>, @value="StartsWithABang writes Thanks to the fact that the Moon is tidally locked, we can only see 50% of its surface on any given night. Over time, the fact that the Moon&#39;s orbit is elliptical, and that it moves faster at perigee and slower at apogee means that up to another 9% is visible over the course of many years. The observed &quot;rocking&quot; and growing/shrinking of the Moon over time is known as lunar libration, an incredibly interesting phenomenon. But now, for the first time, we&#39;ve been able to visualize how the Earth appears to move as seen from above the far side of the Moon.&lt;p&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;share_submission&quot; seems to be volcanic ash, though ash from which volcano isn&#39;t completely clear. Experts said they are checking out several possible explanations including a recent volcanic eruption in Mexico and one in Russia. The weather service said the rainstorm may have passed through some dust or volcanic ash as it moved west. Walla Walla County&#39;s emergency management staff posted a statement on its Facebook page that the ash is likely from Volcano Shiveluch in Kamchatka Krai, Russia, some 3,000 miles away. Volcano Shiveluch spewed an ash plume about 22,000 feet high in late January, the statement said.... CNN meteorologist Derek Van Dam, meanwhile, pointed to an eruption Wednesday of a volcano in southwestern Colima, Mexico, as another potential source of the dirty rain. That volcano is more than 2,000 miles away from the region. #<Axlsx::Cell:0x007fc1e8982248 @row=#<Axlsx::Row:0x007fc1e8982810 ...>, @value="mikejuk writes A plan is afoot to replace the Turing test as a measure of a computer&#39;s ability to think. The idea is for an annual or bi-annual Turing Championship consisting of three to five different challenging tasks. A recent workshop at the 2015 AAAI Conference of Artificial Intelligence was chaired by Gary Marcus, a professor of psychology at New York University. His opinion is that the Turing Test had reached its expiry date and has become &quot;an exercise in deception and evasion.&quot; Marcus points out: the real value of the Turing Test comes from the sense of competition it sparks amongst programmers and engineers which has motivated the new initiative for a multi-task competition. The one of the tasks is based on Winograd Schemas. This requires participants to grasp the meaning of sentences that are easy for humans to understand through their knowledge of the world. One simple example is: &quot;The trophy would not fit in the brown suitcase because it was too big. What was too big?&quot; Another suggestion is for the program to answer questions about a TV program: No existing program &amp;mdash; not Watson, not Goostman, not Siri &amp;mdash; can currently come close to doing what any bright, real teenager can do: watch an episode of &quot;The Simpsons,&quot; and tell us when to laugh. Another is called the &quot;Ikea&quot; challenge and asks for robots to co-operate with humans to build flat-pack furniture. This involves interpreting written instructions, choosing the right piece, and holding it in just the right position for a human teammate. This at least is a useful skill that might encourage us to welcome machines into our homes.&lt;p&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;share_submission&quot; style=&quot;position:relative;&quot;&gt; &lt;a
